**Expanding** **yin-yang** to **release** **qi**.

**Separate** and **unite**—
**Heaven** and **Earth** **complete**.
**Heaven** **revolves**, **yang** and **yin** **interact**.
**Return** to **origin**—
**Beginning** and **end** **settled**.

**One** **birth**, **one** **death**—
**Nature** and **life** **refined**.

**Heaven** **divides** **yang** **above**,
Thus **sun**, **moon**, **Five Stars** **adorn** it—
All **yin** **within**.

**Gazing** upward to **patterns**,
**Gazing** downward to **emotions**.
**Discerning** **nature**, **knowing** **fate**,
**Tracing** **origins**, **seeing** **ends**.

**Three** **Principles**—**shared** **nature**,
**Thick** and **thin** **contrasting**.

**Round**—**sturdy** and **flexible**,
**Square**—**stingy** and **parsimonious**.

**Exhale**—**fluid** **form**,
**Inhale**—**doubtful** **shape**.

Thus **enclosing** **Heaven** is called **Space**,
**Opening** **Space** is called **Duration**.
**Enclosing** **Heaven**—**Space**;
**Opening** **Space**—**Duration**.

**One** **yang**, **one** **yin**—
**Heaven’s** and **Earth’s** **transformation**.
**Sun** and **moon** **passing**—
**One** **cold**, **one** **hot**.

**Calendars** **record** **time**.
**Music** and **calendars** **intertwine**—

**Night**—**despised**.

**Yin** and **yang** **distinguished**.

**Day**—**extreme** **yang**.

**Female**, **male**, **pure**—
**Expanding** **auspicious** and **inauspicious**.

Thus **sovereign**, **minister**, **father**, **son**,
**husband**, **wife**—**distinguished**.

Hence **sun** **moves** **eastward**,
**Heaven** **moves** **westward**.
**Heaven** and **sun** **interweave**,
**Yin** and **yang** **cycle**.

**Death** and **life** **entangled**—
**Ten thousand things** **ensnared**.

Thus **Mysterious** **gathers** **Heaven’s** **unified** **connections**.

**Only** the **Mysterious** does so.

*Obscure*—*Shìwén* reads *wǔ* (膴), **dim**.

Others read *huìhuì*.

**Mysterious**—
**Obscuring** its **position**, **blurring** its **boundaries**,

Thus **Mysterious** **stands** **distant** before **all**,
**Vast** and **expansive**,
**Deep** and **profound**,
**Faint** and **vanishing**.

**Harmonizing** all—**Mysterious**.

**It is humanity that scatters** **it**—
**Knocking at its gate**, **opening its doors**, **striking its keys**—
**Only then does it respond**.
**How much less** when it **denies**?

**For those who cultivate the Mysterious**—
**Knocking at its outer gate**, **no response**.
**Opening its inner doors**, **no response**.
**Striking its keys in secret**, **only then does it respond**.
**How much less** for those who **do not cultivate**?

**Entering ever deeper**, **seeking ever more sparsely**—
**Then the Mysterious responds**.
**Not that the Mysterious responds to seeking**,
**But that the utmost refinement communicates**.

What **humans** **desire yet lack** is **virtue**;
What **humans** **abhor yet possess in excess** is **vice**.
The **Noble One**, **strengthening what is lacking**,
**Diminishing what is in excess**—
**Thus approaches the Dao of the Mysterious**.

**Gazing upward**, it **resides above**;
**Gazing downward**, it **peeks below**;
**Straining forward**, it **lies ahead**;
**Turning back**, it **vanishes behind**.
**Attempting to evade it is impossible**—
**Silently attaining its place**—
**This is the Mysterious**.

**Daily strengthening virtue** while **diminishing vice**,
**To perfect virtue and instrumentality**—
**That is all**.

**If the Mysterious**, then **await its silent accord**.
**Approaching the Dao**,
**What is lacking is filled and flourishes**,
**What is in excess is removed and does not obscure**—
**Thus entering the Mysterious’ equilibrium**.

**Therefore, the Mysterious**—
**Its use is consummate**.

**Able to pair with all things**—**this is harmony**;
**Unbound by attachments**—**this is sagacity**;
**Timing and untiming**—**this is fate**.

**The Void Form**—
**The Way through which ten thousand things pass**—
**Is called the Way**.

*Song*, *Lin*, *Xu*, and *Huang* read *xūwúxíng*.

**Is called the Way**—*Song* and *Xu*, *Huang* originally include *zhī* ("that"),

**Is called virtue**.

**The Mysterious**—
**It balances and measures**.

**Speaking of the Mysterious’ rectitude**,
**Exceeding human affairs**—**thus**.

**Vastly displaying its divine mystery**;

**To harmonize the *Xuanji*’s order**,
**And rectify the *Yùhéng*’s equilibrium**.

**Hard and soft** **interacting**.

**When full, it enters decay**,
**When exhausted, it renews**.
**Having substance, having emptiness**,
**Flow and cessation without constancy**.

**Speaking of the Mysterious’ alignment with the Seven Governors**,
**To mirror Heaven and Earth**—**thus**.

**Thus nobility and humility are ordered**.

**Thus ruler and subject are rightly aligned**.

**Thus all affairs are distinguished**.

**Thus presence and absence are clear**.

**Thus good and evil are evident**.
**Void and substance surge**,
**Thus all things are entangled**.
**Yang not reaching its extreme, Yin does not sprout**,
**Yin not reaching its extreme, Yang does not emerge**.
**Extreme cold generates heat**, **extreme heat generates cold**.
**Trusting the Dao leads to bending**,
**Bending the Dao leads to trust**.

**In its motion**, **daily creating what is not**,
**And delighting in what is new**.
**In its stillness**, **daily diminishing what is done**,
**And reducing what is accomplished**.

**Thus probing with the *kè*** (刻),
**Comparing with the *guǐ*** (晷),
**Reversing its sequence**,
**Turning its Way**—
**To reveal the unseen Form**,
**To draw the unspun thread**,
**And connect with all kinds**.

**Above, it suspends Heaven**,
**Below, it sinks into the abyss**,
**Fine, it enters the reeds** (秽),
**Broad, it encompasses the *zhěn*** (轸).

**Its Dao**—**obscure and deep**—
**Fills what is full**—*Ding* and *Song* read *yāyíng*.

**Preserving while perishing**,
**Faint yet manifest**,
**Beginning while ending**—
**Near the Mysterious, the Mysterious draws near**;
**Far from the Mysterious, the Mysterious withdraws**.

**Like Heaven, vast and blue**,
**Present in the east, south, west, and north**,
**Gazing upward, none are absent**,
**Yet when lowered, it is unseen**.
**Does Heaven truly depart from humanity?**
**It is humanity that departs from it**.

**The Winter Solstice and the hours after midnight**—
**Symbols of nearing the Mysterious**.

**Advancing yet unexhausted**,
**Going yet unreached**,
**Empty yet unfilled**—
**Thus called nearing the Mysterious**.

「The Summer Solstice and the hours after midday—
**Symbols of withdrawing from the Mysterious**.

Advancing to its utmost and then receding,
Proceeding to exhaustion and then returning,
Filled to capacity and then diminished—
Thus called withdrawing from the Mysterious.

When the sun turns southward, all things die;
When the sun turns northward, all things live.

When the Dipper** (斗) turns northward, all things grow **empty** (虚);
When the Dipper turns southward, all things grow **full** (盈).
The sun’s southern turn—
**Rightward in motion, leftward in return**;
The Dipper’s southern turn—
**Leftward in motion, rightward in return**.

Sometimes left, sometimes right,
Sometimes death, sometimes life—
**The Mysterious and the numinous** conspire together,
**Heaven and Earth** thus align,
**Heaven’s numinous** and **Earth’s spirit** (灵).

**The Mysterious Dao** is such—
Thus, through human affairs and transformations of things,
It **harmonizes with Heaven and Earth**,
**Unified without division**,
And the Mysterious stands as its **apex** (宗).

On the Summer Solstice, the sun reaches its southernmost point at **Eastern Well** (东井);
On the Winter Solstice, the sun reaches its northernmost point at **The Ox Driver** (牵牛).
The Dipper **governs the four seasons**,
Each establishing its own direction.
The sun **traverses the western sky and returns eastward**,
The Dipper **reaches the eastern sky and returns westward**.

All things depend upon it—
When full, the signs of death appear;
When empty, new life emerges.
The Mysterious **scatters as one yin and one yang**,
Its **movements**—left and right—**meet in opposition**.
Thus, it **unifies the Mysterious and the numinous**,
And **returns to the primal wholeness of the Mysterious**.

It is said, **"Heaven’s numinous and Earth’s spirit"**,
Meaning **unified yet not chaotic**,
**The Mysterious** **illuminates** **Heaven and Earth’s transformations**,
**Encompassing all without obstruction**.

(In some texts, *zhāng* and *dīng* read *wàng* instead of *nèi*.)
**The beginning and the end**—**profound and luminous**—
**Exalt the Mysterious and the numinous**,
**The Great Yang** **rides upon the yin**,
All things **comprehensively included**,
**Circulating through the Nine Voids** (九虚),
And **weaving fate and fortune** (祸福).

In the **twelve beginnings** (十二始),
All affairs **unravel their threads**,
Thus there are **one, two, three**,
To **weave and measure** (絓罗),
And the Mysterious Dao **illuminates** them.

**The Five Phases** (五行) **originate from the Dipper**,
With **nine positions** **repeatedly applied** (重施).
Above and below **interact in sequence**,
And **the Ugly** (丑) **lies within**—
The Mysterious Dao **illuminates** it.

**Heaven’s Garden** (天园) **spreads across the four directions**,
**Central Planting** (极植) **established at the heart**,
**Movement governed by stillness** (动以历静),
**Time measured in twelve**,
To **found the Seven Celestial Officials** (七政)—
The Mysterious Dao **illuminates** it.

The Dipper **shakes Heaven and advances**,
The sun **defies Heaven and retreats**,
Sometimes **shaken**, sometimes **defiant**—
To **establish the Five Epochs** (五纪)—
The Mysterious Dao **illuminates** it.

**Planting and measuring** (植表) **cast their shadows** (施景),
**Willow and Mulberry** (榆与株) **marked by their cuts** (切).

**The water clock’s rate** (漏率) **is measured by the gnomon** (刻),
**Dusk and dawn** (昏明) **are gauged at the midpoint** (考中),
The **observers use the gnomon** (以戒)—
The Mysterious Dao **illuminates** it.

**Cold bamboo** (冷竹) **as the tube** (管),
**Ash from the hearth** (室灰) **as the marker** (候),
To **investigate all undertakings** (揆百度).
When the **undertakings are set**,
The **people are aided without delay**—
The Mysterious Dao **illuminates** it.

**East and west as the weft** (纬),
**South and north as the warp** (经),
**Warp and weft intersecting**,
**Distinguishing perverse and orthodox** (邪正),
**Revealing auspicious and inauspicious** (吉凶)—
The Mysterious Dao **illuminates** it.

**Digging wells** (凿井) **to draw clear water** (澹水),
**Boring fire** (钻火) **and carving wood** (难木),
**Melting metal and molding clay** (流金陶土),
To **blend the Five Refined Arts** (五美).
The **resources of the Five Refined Arts**,
To **nourish all bodies** (资百体)—
The Mysterious Dao **illuminates** it.

**Odd numbers** (奇) **measure yang**,
**Even numbers** (耦) **measure yin**,
**Odd and even** **pushed and performed**,
To **calculate all under Heaven**—
The Mysterious Dao **illuminates** it.

**Six beginnings** (六始) **as the laws** (律),
**Six intervals** (六间) **as the harmonics** (吕),
When **laws and harmonics** are **coordinated**,
The **twelve** are **tuned**,
And **daytime and nighttime** are **measured**—
The Mysterious Dao **illuminates** it.

**The Eighty-One Divisions** (八十一所) **of the states and families**,
**Marked as lower, middle, and upper**,
To **represent the Four Seas**—
The Mysterious Dao **illuminates** it.

**One division** (一辟),
**Three ministers** (三公),
**Nine officials** (九卿),
**Twenty-seven great officers** (二十七大夫),
**Eighty-one elemental officials** (八十一元士)—
**Few govern the many**,
**None govern the nonexistent**—
The Mysterious Dao **illuminates** it.

In ancient times, **there were no thunder sacrifices** (不霆) **nor divinations** (不虞),
(In some texts, *lèi* is read *yú* instead of *pèi*—
Sound: *yú*, others read *lèi*.)
**Slowing their contemplations** (慎其思虑),
**Not relying on fortune-telling or augury** (匪筮匪卜),
When **auspicious and inauspicious** **intermingled**,
The **sages** then **crafted the Yarrow Stalk and tortoise shell**,
**Piercing the essence** (钻精) **and leaning upon the spirit** (倚神),
**Clasping knowledge** (箝知) **of rest and auspice** (休咎)—
The Mysterious Dao **illuminates** it.

Thus, to **know what is unknowable**,
One **approximates it through the trigrams and hexagrams** (卦兆),
To **fathom depths and trace distances**,
One **seeks it through contemplation** (思虑).
Of these two, which **establishes the essence**?
The **essence** in **fortune-telling and divination**,
**The spirit moves its changes**;
The **essence** in **contemplation**,
**Plans align with their fittingness**;
The **essence** in **upright establishment**,
**None can overthrow it**;
The **essence** in **having what is guarded**,
**None can seize it**.
Thus, to **unravel the tangled threads** (抽天下之蔓蔓)
And **dispel the chaotic mixtures** (散天下之混混)
Under Heaven—
Who but the **essence** could accomplish this?

**Illuminating from self-measurement** (莹自度数),
**Radiant in all methods** (晖於诸法),
And **chiefly relying on the utmost precision** (至精者),
It **returns to the One**.

The **observers**,
**Value adherence to natural patterns** (循) **and embodying spontaneity** (体自然).
When their **adherence is vast**,
Then their **embodiment is robust** (壮);
When their **adherence is slight**,
Then their **embodiment is meager** (瘠).
When their **adherence is straight**,
Then their **embodiment is complete** (浑);
When their **adherence is crooked**,
Then their **embodiment is scattered** (散).
Thus, they **do not fear what they possess**,
Nor **force what they lack**.
Like the **body itself**,
**Adding causes excess** (赘),
**Removing causes deficiency** (亏).
Thus, **substance is guided by nature** (质斡),
**Embellishment by human affairs** (华藻)—
Can it be **augmented or diminished**?

(The original reads: *"华藻在乎人事也，其可损益与？"*
Some texts omit *人事*, reading instead: *"华藻其作其字"*—
The **allowance** and **yellowing** **are as they are**.)

The **One** is **used to trace beginnings** (摹始)
And **measure depths** (测深),
The **three threes** (三三) **to exhaust endings** (尽终)
And **reach the utmost heights** (极崇),
The **two twos** (二二) **to align affairs** (参事)
And **grasp the central way** (要中).
**Human affairs mirror this**,
**Dedicating to its work** (务其事)
**Not its words** (不务其辞),
**Multiplying its changes** (多其变)
**Not its forms** (不多其文).

**Without coordination**, its **intentions are unclear** (其指不详),
**Without centrality**, its **responses are narrow** (其应不博),
**Without completeness**, its **work is confined** (其事不散),
**Without depth**, its **meaning is unseen** (其意不见).
Thus, **forms reveal the substance** (文以见乎质),
**Words reveal the emotions** (辞以睹乎情).
By **observing its application of words**,
One **sees what its heart desires**.

Such are the **words of the Mysterious Dao**.
**Exalting the Nine Degrees** (九度):
**One-One** (一一),
**One-Two** (一二),
**One-One-Two** (一一二),
**Two-One** (二一),
**Two-Two** (二二),
**Two-Three** (二三),
**Three-One** (三一),
**Three-Two** (三二),
**Three-Three** (三三).

**One-One** is the **beginning**; **Three-Three**, the **apex**; **Two-Two**, the **center**.
This is the **unalterable natural measure**—
a model for **divination’s calculations**.

The **Dao** has **roots and continuity**, **transformation and change**.
Following roots and continuity—**harmony with the Dao’s spirit**;
Transforming and changing—**adapting to the times**.
Thus, **rooted yet transformative**, the **Heavenly Dao is realized**;
**Transformative yet rooted**, the **Heavenly Dao is tamed**.

Things **do not arise without roots**, nor **fulfill without transformation**.
Thus, **knowing roots but not transformation**, things **lose their standard**;
**Knowing transformation but not roots**, things **lose their balance**.
Transformation **untimely**, things **lose their foundation**;
Roots **unprincipled**, things **lose their order**.

**Rooting and transforming**—
the **measures of statecraft**.
The **movement of measures**—
the **effects of success and failure**.

**Adaptability**—
the **mysteries of the Dao**.

Roots **mirror water and wood**,
Transformation **mirrors metal and fire**.

Establishing **Heaven’s threads**—
**Yin and Yang** are called;
Shaping **Earth’s weaves**—
**Compliance and Resistance** are called;
Manifesting **human conduct**—
**Obscurity and Clarity** are called.

**Yin and Yang**—**uniting their distinctions**;
**Compliance and Resistance**—**weaving the threads**;
**Obscurity and Clarity**—**discriminating their essence**.

Yin without Yang—**no union in application**;
Threads without weaves—**no fulfillment in meaning**;
Clarity without Obscurity—**no distinction in virtue**.

**Yin and Yang**—**to draw forth emotions**;
**Compliance and Resistance**—**to refine principles**;
**Obscurity and Clarity**—**to illuminate affairs**.

**Drawing emotions**—**the refined Dao**;
**Refining principles**—**the illuminated conduct**;
**Illuminating affairs**—**the path of the virtuous**.

**Opening to its name**—
the **mysteries’ speech**.

From the **center as Yang**, encircling as **Yin**,
to **extreme the eighty-one heads**.

Nine positions at the **center**,
threads and weaves intersecting—
things **manifest their meaning** as they encounter time.

**Obscurity and Clarity**—
the **matters of day and night**.

**Coming and going**, **permeating**—
entering the **Gate of Loss**.

**What is gained and what is lost**—
**gaining blessings, losing calamities**.

Heaven and Earth:
**Blessings align**, calamities **reverse**;
Mountains and rivers:
**Blessings settle low**, calamities **rise high**;
Human conduct:
**Blessings are upright**, calamities **are perverse**.

Thus, the **virtuous**—
**internally upright, externally tamed**,
**always yielding to others**—
therefore **their actions gain blessings and avoid calamities**.

Blessings **do not arise from ugliness**,
calamities **do not persist from goodness**.
**Ugliness and goodness**—
the **virtuous thus clearly distinguish**.

Blessings **end in joy**, calamities **begin in sorrow**.
What Heaven and Earth **value** is called **blessing**;
what **ghosts and spirits** **favor** is called **blessing**;
what **human conduct** **delights in** is called **blessing**;
what they **despise and abhor**—all are called **calamity**.

Thus, the **more one despises blessings**, the **greater the calamity**.
The **calamities of daytime** are few—**pure in clarity**;
the **calamities of night** are many—**pure in obscurity**.
Those **scattered between day and night**—
their **calamities and blessings mix**,
for they are **neither purely obscure nor purely clear**.

**Refining to illuminate affairs**—
to make people **know the return of calamities and blessings**.

---
**太玄数卷第八 玄数**

**Kunlun**—**Heaven and Earth’s birthplace**—**produces the stalks**,
**three sacred essences** **refined**—**to number**.

Dispersing the **mysterious in three layers** to establish **families**,
**comparing the Two Principles** to **perceive affairs**.

**Encounters and unions**—
**naming their patterns** and **extending their command**.

**Precision**—**the threads of doubt**—**its substance revealed**.
**The Oracle says**: *"Assume the Great Mysteries"*.

**Assuming the Great Mysteries**—**truth and sincerity**,
**doubting the substance**—**divine and spirit-like**.

**Rest**—**encountering Yang**, stars and times **align in speech**;
**Blame**—**encountering Yin**, stars and times **contradict in speech**.

**Divination has its Dao**:
**Without precision, do not divinate**,
**without doubt, do not divinate**,
**without order, do not divinate**,
**without its omens, do not divinate as if divining**.

**Divine brilliance**—**soaring beyond** (three characters repeated).
**Thirty-six**—**the stalks are viewed**.

Heaven **divides by three**, completing **six**—
thus **eighteen stalks**.

Heaven **does not act alone**, Earth **does not complete alone**—
**doubling their roots**, Earth **lacks three** to **match Heaven’s eighteen**.

**Separate one** and hang it **on the left small finger**,
**dividing the rest in half**.

With three stalks gathered, the remainder is grouped under **艻** [same as *扐*].
After one **艻**, recount the rest in sevens—seven as one, eight as two, nine as three—
thus six counts exhaust the **stalks’ Dao**.

**Encountering** has **lower, middle, upper**:
Lower is **thought**,
Middle is **fortune**,
Upper is **calamity**.
Thought, fortune, and calamity each have lower, middle, upper—
by day and night, their **rest and blame** are distinguished.

Heaven divides by three, thus one, two, three **weave into six**.
Multiply six by three to make **eighteen**.
Heaven acts, Earth completes it—
thus doubled, they form **thirty-six**.
This is the **divine brilliance**—**soaring beyond** (three characters repeated).

Earth lacks three to match Heaven’s eighteen—
thus the stalks use **thirty-three**.

The **Mysterious Divination** hangs one stalk—**most precise**;
dividing and gathering three times—**most variable**;
grouping the remainder under **艻**—**returning to the odd**.

After one **艻**, recounting the rest yields seven, eight, or nine—
thus day’s one, two, three.

Heaven completes six, so six counts exhaust the **stalks’ Dao**—
numbers reach their limit, symbols find their fullness.

Obtain **direction**, seek **province**, obtain **department**, seek **house**—
this is **dispersing the obscure through three layers** and establishing **house**—**fourfold**.

Extreme one becomes two, extreme two becomes three, extreme three becomes **推** [*tuī*],
**推** three becomes **嬴赞** [*yíngzàn*].
*Chapter, Xu*, and *Ding* variants read **推** three as **赢赞**—
*嬴* or *赢* are interchangeable.
*赞嬴* enters **表**, *表嬴* enters **家**, *家嬴* enters **部**, *部嬴* enters **州**, *州嬴* enters **方**.
*Fàn Zhǔ* notes: *玄* may be *去* [omitted].
*Lù Yún* says: Should read *玄*.
Now all versions read *玄*, except *Sòng* as *去*, *Chapter* as *入玄*.
Numbers arise from *玄*, extend to extremes, then return to *玄*.
This is how the Sage harmonizes the people’s **fortune and calamity**,
washing the heart in secrecy—
thus interspersed within the **divination method**.

In ancient times, **Yú** divided the nine provinces,
assigned tributes by soil, and bestowed upon **Yáo** the **black jade tablet**,
declaring his success—
symbolizing this very principle.

**One follows, two follow, three follow**—**Great Rest**.
**One follows, two follow, three contradict**—
beginning and middle **Rest**, ending in **blame**.
**One follows, two contradict, three contradict**—
beginning **Rest**, middle and end **blame**.
**One contradicts, two follow, three follow**—
beginning **blame**, middle and end **Rest**.
**One contradicts, two contradict, three follow**—
beginning and middle **blame**, ending in **Rest**.
**One contradicts, two contradict, three contradict**—**Great Blame**.

Divination has four aspects: **stars, times, numbers, speech**.
Morning uses **classics**, evening uses **weft**.
Observe beginning and middle, decide by the end.
Day signifies **Rest**, night signifies **blame**.
And by **stars, times, numbers, speech**—
harmony or contradiction,盛衰—
their categories align to determine the matter.

Morning uses **classics**: one, five, seven;
Evening uses **weft**: three, four, eight;
Morning and evening combined: two **classics**, one **weft**, using two, six, nine—
this is the **three tables**.
Morning symbolizes **Heaven**, evening **Earth**, the middle **Human**.

One, five, six advance to **seven**,
Three, four, seven advance to **eight**,
Two, six, eight advance to **nine**.
Observing beginning and middle, deciding by the end—
examining accumulated extremes and grasping their changes.

Thus the remaining **艻** numbers:
One portends **seven**, three portends **eight**, two portends **nine**.

Divination may yield **ending Rest but reversing blame**,
or **ending blame but reversing Rest**—
it depends on carefully observing the questioned matter,
cross-referencing with **stars, times, numbers**.

If not a matter of **loyalty and sincerity**, fortune may shift to misfortune—
this is the **divination law**.

**Three eights** are **Wood**, the **East**, **Spring**.
Days: **Jia, Yi**; hours: **Yín, Mǎo**.
Sound: **Jué (角)**, color: **green**, taste: **sour**, odor: **rancid**, form: **bent and trustworthy**.
Generates **Fire**, overcomes **Earth**.
Seasonally generates, stores in the **spleen**.
The **lung** extends upward to cover the **kidney**,
descends low to conceal the **heart**,
resides centrally to embody **sovereign virtue**,
while **spleen (left)** and **liver (right)** support the **Five Phases** in position.

*The Monthly Ordinances* decree:
Spring sacrifices to the **spleen**, summer to the **lung**,
Central (autumn?) sacrifices to the **heart**, autumn to the **liver**,
Winter to the **kidney**—
this is the **Mysterious Correspondence**.

Thus the **lung** stores **qi**—**Fire**;
the **kidney** stores **essence**—**Water**;
the **heart** stores **spirit**—**Earth**;
the **spleen** stores **thought**—**Wood**;
the **liver** stores **blood**—**Metal**.

As **bodies**, they are:
**Spleen (Earth)**, **Lung (Metal)**, **Heart (Fire)**, **Liver (Wood)**, **Kidney (Water)**;
As **positions**, they **nourish and govern**, **minister and domesticate**.

Not aligning with others—**one alone**—
the **Mysterious Virtue’s** symbol.

**Preserve intent (志)**, **preserve sound (音)** [or *store*].
Wood preserves **intent**—**uprightness**;
Metal preserves **ether (魄)**—**campaigning**;
Fire preserves **soul (魂)**—**transformation**;
Water preserves **essence**—**concealment**;
Earth preserves **spirit**—**transmutation**.
**Intent** is **Water**, yet stored in **Wood**;
**Ether** is **Earth**, yet stored in **Metal**;
**Soul** is **Wood**, yet stored in **Fire**;
**Spirit** is **Fire**, yet stored in **Earth**.
All entrust themselves to their **generative source**.

As *Laozi* says:
*"Weaken the intent, strengthen the bones,
empty the heart, fill the belly."*
Only the **perfectly unified** remain undivided.

**Nature** is **benevolence**, **emotion** is **joy**.
**Affairs** appear **proper**, **conduct** is **reverent**,
**solemn**, **austere**, **drought**.
*The Hong Fan* records:
*"Rain and drought follow weft,
heat and cold, wind follow classics."*

**Mysterious numbers** classify by their **true names** alone—
not by **clashing qi** intermingling.

**Emperor Tàiwú**, **God Gōumáng**—
**stars** follow their positions.
**Shì, Fáng, Xīn, Wěi, Jī**—
positions **Yín, Mǎo**.
Their **categories** include:
**scales**, **thunder**, **drums**, **resounding sound**, **novelty**, **restlessness**, **door**, **window**.

「The **Tàixiàng** (甲象) scales as **lín** (鳞),
in orderly ranks, their abundance grows.
When pushed to their utmost, they **zhèn** (震) and transform into **léi** (雷)—thunder,
into **gǔ** (鼓)—drums,
into **huīshēng** (恢声)—resounding echoes.

Their emergence marks **xīn** (新)—novelty,
their obstruction yields **zào** (躁)—restlessness.
The grand becomes **hù** (户)—door, and exits,
the small becomes **yǒu** (牖)—window, and flows through.
All things:
to exit, they must pass through **hù** (户),
to enter, they must pass through **mén** (门).
**Hù** (户) is **odd** (奇),
**mén** (门) is **even** (偶).

The **zào** (灶) stove and **tì** (惕) hearth nurture by **liú** (流通)—circulation,
while the **zhōngliú** (中溜) central hearth
**chōng** (冲) and **xū** (虚) to clear the **hán** (函)—enclosure,
illuminating **tiān** (天)—Heaven,
and receiving all **liú** (流).
Thus, this **fú** (福)—blessing is gathered,
and the family master presides over it.

When doors and stoves open and close in change,
this is **wéi** (纬)—the **subtle, responsive** (纬) principle;
when the stove’s circulation and central hearth maintain constancy,
this is **jīng** (经)—the **fundamental, enduring** (经) principle.

Therefore, *The Yueling* (月令) states:
*"In spring, sacrifice to the **hù** (户)—door;
in summer, sacrifice to the **zào** (灶)—stove;
in the center, sacrifice to the **zhōngliú** (中溜)—central hearth;
in autumn, sacrifice to the **mén** (门)—gate;
in winter, sacrifice to the **xíng** (行)—circulation."*

Their **categories** (类) align with the **Wǔwù** (五物)—five elements,
harmonizing with the **Mysterious Numbers** (玄).
To **sì** (嗣)—inherit,
to **chéng** (承)—uphold,
to **yè** (叶)—follow,
to **xù** (绪)—continue.
**Zhèn** (震) as the **chángzǐ** (长子)—eldest son’s transformation.

To become **hù** (户) and **yǒu** (牖),
then the family is established.
To **shè** (赦)—pardon,
to **jiě** (解)—release,
and to bear **duōzǐ** (多子)—many offspring.
The **shuì** (税) of witheredness and the **jiè** (枯) of decay,
the **shì** (释) of shedding and the **jiǎ** (甲) of scales—
these are the **zhèn** (震) element’s functions,
mirrored in state affairs.

**Méngshēng** (萌生) sprouting and **yùnzì** (孕字) bearing—
the season’s bounty flourishes.
To **chū** (出)—emerge,
to **yǔ** (予)—bestow.
The **Emperor** (帝) emerges from **zhèn** (震),
spreading **virtue/power** (德) and **bestowing benevolence** (施惠),
while all things take form accordingly.
To **shè** (赦)—pardon and **jiě** (解)—release,
is to emerge and bestow.

To **zhú** (竹)—bamboo and **cǎo** (草)—grass,
to **guǒ** (果)—fruit and **shí** (实)—kernel.
**Xiùbá** (秀拔) refined and **pú** (拔) towering, they become **zhú** (竹)—bamboo;
**zīmàn** (滋蔓) spreading and **wàn** (蔓) creeping, they become **cǎo** (草)—grass.
**Shǒuliǎn** (首敛) concentrated at the head, they become **guǒ** (果)—fruit,
all **mùqì** (木气)—wood **qi**.
Fruit becomes **shí** (实)—kernel,
and the kernel’s form suggests rebirth.

To become **yú** (鱼)—fish:
water nurtures **línshǔ** (鳞属)—scaled creatures,
a symbol of **fánxī** (蕃息)—proliferation and growth.
From bamboo and grass to fish,
all belong to the **duōzǐ** (多子)—many offspring category.

To become **shūqì** (疏器)—perforated vessels.
*The Yueling* (月令) states:
*"In spring, their vessels are perforated to allow passage."*
**Kè** (刻) carved and **lòu** (镂) hollowed,
symbolizing the **tǔ** (土) element’s unrestricted emergence.
Perforated vessels **zhì** (致) harness human effort
to correspond with **tiānshí** (天时)—Heaven’s seasons.

To become **tián** (田)—field and **guī** (规)—boundary:
**Xǔ** (许) and **Huáng** (黄) as boundaries form fields,
**Sòng** (宋) and **Guō** (郭) as fields define boundaries.
**Mù** (木) governs **tǔ** (土).
To become **tián** (田)—field,
**mù** (木) takes charge, and the **jìguān** (稷官) officials expand their cultivation.
To become **guī** (规)—boundary,
it mirrors the **yuán** (元) principle’s **yùnmù** (运木)—circulation of wood.
**Tǔ** (土) rests upon the wood’s **jī** (稽)—foundation,
symbolizing the exertion of effort in spring
to harmonize with Heaven’s bounty.

To become **máo** (矛)—spear:
**Jùbīng** (句兵) weapons bend without piercing.
**Gēshì** (戈氏) **yīn** (罇) and **máoshì** (矛氏) **tuì** (镦).
The **máo** (矛) is **dūn** (敦)—thick, symbolizing **rén** (仁)—benevolence.
To become **qīngguài** (青怪)—strange and green:
**Zhèng** (正) governs the state,
**qí** (奇) is used in warfare.
When the **Wǔxíng** (五行)—five elements
**fǎncháng** (反常)—reverse their usual order,
each displays its **yì** (异)—unusual aspect.

To become **bì** (鼽)—nasal congestion:
**yīnqiú** (音求)—sound seeks resonance.
When **spring’s xíng** (行) overlaps with **autumn’s lìng** (令),
people suffer **bì** (鼽)—nasal congestion,
as **jīn** (金) **zhì** (沴) overcomes **mù** (木).
To become **kuáng** (狂)—madness:
**fúgōngfúsù** (弗恭弗肃)—lacking reverence and solemnity,
the excess of **dòngdàng** (动荡)—turbulence.
**Sìjiǔ** (四九) the **fourth phase of the ninth month** (四九) corresponds to **jīn** (金),
to the **west** (西方),
to **autumn** (秋).
**Dì** (日) **gēngxīn** (庚辛),
**shènyǒuxiǔ** (辰申酉).
**Shēngshāng** (声商)—sound of the **Shāng** (商) tone,
**sèbái** (色白)—white hue,
**wèixīn** (味辛)—pungent flavor,
**xiùxīng** (臭腥)—fishy odor,
**xínggé** (形革)—leathery form.
It **shēng** (生) produces **water** (水),
**shèng** (胜) overcomes **wood** (木).
**Shíkè** (时杀)—seasonal restraint,
**cánggān** (藏肝)—conceals the liver,
**cúnpò** (存魄)—preserves the **pò** (魄)—etheric soul.
**Xìngyì** (性谊)—nature of **yì** (谊)—harmony,
**qíngnù** (情怒)—passion of anger.
**Shìyán** (事言)—affairs of speech,
**yòngcóng** (用从)—conduct of compliance,
**sùyì** (撝乂)—solemn and **yì** (乂)—restrained.
**Zhèngyǔ** (征雨)—summons rain.
**Dìshǎowú** (帝少吴),
**Shénsuǎnshōu** (神蓐收),
**xīngcóngqìwèi** (星从其位)—stars follow their positions.
**Wèi, Mǎo, Bì, Shì, Shēn** (胃、昴、毕、氏、参),
**wèishēnyǒuxiǔ** (位申酉).
Their **categories** (类) include **máo** (毛)—hair.
**Jīn** (金) **géhuǒ** (革火)—transforms fire,
and **shōu** (收)—concentrates it,
its **qì** (气) disperses and spreads.
To become **máo** (毛)—hair,
**gēngxīn** (庚辛) **xiàng** (象)—symbolism prevails.
To become **yī** (医)—physician,
**wūzhù** (巫祝)—shaman and diviner,
and **měng** (猛)—fierce.
**Tángrén** (唐人) avoided taboo,
often rewriting **hǔ** (虎)—tiger as **měng** (猛).
This character likely should be **hǔ** (虎),
though no original text confirms it.

To become **jiù** (旧)—old,
and **míng** (鸣)—sound.
**Yī** (医) attacks **jí** (疾)—illness,
**wūzhù** (巫祝) invoke the **bèibùxiǎng** (被不详)—unclear mysteries,
both skilled in **gé** (革)—transformation.
To become **měng** (猛)—fierce,
it is **hǔ** (虎)—tiger,
a **jiǎmáo** (甲毛) category of scales and hair.
The **hǔ** (虎) tiger transforms into **yìlóng** (异龙)—strange dragon,
its **jīnjiù** (因旧) reliance on the old
brings **bǐng** (炳)—radiance.
All things, once fully formed, **míng** (鸣)—resound,
as the tiger’s roar echoes through the wind—
the **shèng** (盛)—peak of sound.
The physician’s **gé** (革)—transformative work
restores the **jiù** (旧)—old order,
while shamans and diviners excel in **míng** (鸣)—resonance.
When things are **zhèng** (正)—proper, they mark **xīn** (新)—new;
when things are **lǎo** (老)—aged, they mark **jiù** (旧)—old.
All movement is **mù** (木)—wood,
all sound is **jīn** (金)—metal.
**Dòngjiá** (动夬) turbulent movement becomes **zào** (躁)—restlessness,
**shēngyáng** (声扬) resonant sound becomes **míng** (鸣)—resonance.
Resonance upholds **jié** (节)—order.
To become **mén** (门)—gate,
**shān** (山)—mountain,
**xiàn** (限)—boundary,
**biān** (边)—edge,
**chéng** (城)—wall,
**gǔ** (骨)—bone,
and **shí** (石)—stone:
with **firmness** (坚) and **establishing order** (立节),
they become **mén** (门)—gate,
**shān** (山)—mountain,
**xiàn** (限)—boundary,
**biān** (边)—edge,
**chéng** (城)—wall.
**Jīn** (金) restrains with **fāng** (方)—rectangle.
**Biān** (边) are the **sìfāng** (四方)—four directions,
**chéng** (城) the **sìyíng** (四营)—fortified enclosures,
to create **xiǎn** (险)—defense.
Thus, externally they symbolize **xiàn** (限)—boundary,
**biān** (边)—edge,
and **chéng** (城)—wall.
Internally, they symbolize **gǔ** (骨)—bone.
Bone arises from **firmness** (坚),
this is **mùqì** (木气)—wood **qi**.
Yet all things’ **firmness** (坚) is shaped by **jīn** (金),
so wood’s essence is **bái** (白)—white.
The **jīn** (金) category becomes **gǔ** (骨)—bone,
its extreme is **shí** (石)—stone.

To become **huánpèi** (环佩)—ornaments,
**shǒushì** (首饰)—head adornments,
**zhòngbǎo** (重宝)—precious treasures,
and **dàduō** (大哆)—great **duō** (哆).
*(Note: The **Dīng** (丁) and **Sòng** (宋) versions omit this line.)*

To become **kòuqì** (扣器)—vessels with metal-rimmed mouths.
**Kòu** (扣), pronounced as **kǒu** (口),
adorns vessels’ mouths with **jīn** (金)—metal.
*(Note: Likely the **extreme** (极) of firmness and **shuō** (说)—appeasement,
with **quality** (质) set and **ornament** (文) arising.)*
**Huánpèi** (环佩) are the **jié** (节)—nodes of the body.
**Shǒushì** (首饰) adorn the head,
**zhòngbǎo** (重宝) signify **guì** (贵)—nobility.
**Huánpèi** (环佩) symbolize **sì** (四)—four,
**shǒushì** (首饰) symbolize **jiǔ** (九)—nine.
**Zhòngbǎo** (重宝) embody **juédé** (觉德)—enlightened virtue.
*The Shuōwén Jiězì* (说文) defines **chǐ** (侈) as **dà** (大)—great,
**duō** (哆) as the **duì** (兑)—mouth’s opening.
**Kòuqì** (扣器) adorn vessels’ mouths with metal,
**zhì** (致) to **shuō** (说)—appeasement,
also to **firmness** (立坚).
To become **chōng** (舂)—pestle,
**zhuī** (椎)—mallet,
**lì** (力)—strength,
and **xiàn** (县)—suspend.
*(Note: **Xiàn** (县) is synonymous with **xuán** (悬)—hang.)*
To become **suì** (燧)—flint,
**bīng** (兵)—weapon,
and **xiè** (械)—tool.
To become **chǐ** (齿)—teeth,
**jiǎo** (角)—horns,
**shì** (螫)—sting,
and **dú** (毒)—venom.
**Zhèngshì** (政饰) governs with **shuō** (说)—appeasement,
and **xiǎoguò** (小过) restrains minor excesses.
**Kòuqì** (扣器) receives **shēng** (生)—life.
To become **chōng** (舂)—pestle,
**zhuī** (椎)—mallet,
and **lì** (力)—strength,
to **firmness** (坚) and **shèng** (胜)—overcome.
**Lìshèng** (力胜)—strength overcomes,
then one can **shèng** (胜)—overcome things.
**Xiànzhì** (县之), **xiàn** (县) suspends with **quán** (权)—authority,
**zhì** (制) controlling its **biàn** (变)—trans

呼早切，章作猎。
To be **hū** (呼)—summoned early,
and **zhāng** (章)—hunting.

为寇，为贼，为理，为矩，为金工，为钺。
To become **kòu** (寇)—raider,
**zéi** (贼)—bandit,
**lǐ** (理)—order,
**jǔ** (矩)—compass,
**jīngōng** (金工)—metalworker,
and **yuè** (钺)—axe.

狗守其方，必或入之。
The **hunting dog** (狗) guards its territory,
yet inevitably **intruders** (入) breach it.

为入，纳日也。
To **enter** (入)—to **receive the sun** (纳日).

为取，收岁也。
To **take** (取)—to **harvest the year** (收岁).

为猎，猎时也。
To **hunt** (猎)—to seize the opportune moment (猎时).

猎取之极，为寇，为贼。
When hunting reaches its limit,
it becomes **raider** (寇) and **bandit** (贼).

则理官治之而立方焉，
Then the **official of order** (理官) governs it,
establishing boundaries (立方).

是以为理，为矩。
Thus it becomes **order** (理) and **compass** (矩).

革而从范，故为金工；
When **leather** (革) is cast into a mold,
it becomes the **metalworker** (金工).

弗革而断以义方，则有杀而已，故为钺。
Without leather, but severed by **righteous measure** (义方),
it is merely **slaughter**—thus the **axe** (钺).

兵械以钺，正为金类，专杀焉。
The **weaponry** (兵械) of the axe,
rightly belongs to the **metal category** (金类),
specializing in **slaughter** (杀).

武成左杖黄钺者，示无事於杀故也。
The **Martial Virtue** (武成) wields the **yellow axe** (黄钺) on the left,
showing that **no killing is done in peace**.

为白怪，为喑，为僭。
To become **pale anomaly** (白怪),
**mute** (喑),
and **usurper** (僭).

诸家作赞，丁作僭。
Some texts render it as **praise** (赞),
but **Ding** (丁) renders it as **usurper** (僭).

金反常，则在物为白怪，在人为喑，在国为僭。
When **metal** (金) deviates from its norm,
it becomes **pale anomaly** (白怪) in things,
**mute** (喑) in people,
and **usurper** (僭) in states.

二七为火，为南方，为夏。
**Two sevens** (二七) become **Fire** (火),
the **Southern Direction** (南方),
and **Summer** (夏).

日丙丁，辰巳午。
Days: **Bing** (丙) and **Ding** (丁),
Hours: **Chen** (辰), **Si** (巳), **Wu** (午).

声征，色赤，味苦，臭焦，形上。
Its **sound** (声) is **Zheng** (征),
**color** (色) is **red** (赤),
**taste** (味) is **bitter** (苦),
**odor** (臭) is **scorched** (焦),
and its **form** (形) is **elevated** (上).

生土，胜金。
It **nourishes earth** (生土),
and **overcomes metal** (胜金).

时养，藏肺，传魂。
Its **season** (时) is **nourishing** (养),
it **stores in the lungs** (藏肺),
and **transmits the soul** (传魂).

性礼，情乐。
Its **nature** (性) is **ritual** (礼),
its **emotion** (情) is **joy** (乐).

事视，用明，撝哲。
Its **affairs** (事) are **vision** (视),
its **utility** (用) is **clarity** (明),
and its **augury** (撝) is **wise** (哲).

征热，帝炎帝，神祝融，星从其位。
Its **auspice** (征) is **heat** (热),
its **Emperor** (帝) is **Yan Di** (炎帝),
its **Deity** (神) is **Zhùróng** (祝融),
and its **stars** (星) follow their positions (从其位).

柳、星、张、翼、轸，位巳午。
Stars: **Liu** (柳), **Xing** (星), **Zhang** (张), **Yi** (翼), **Zhen** (轸),
positioned at **Si** (巳) and **Wu** (午).

类为羽，为灶，为丝，为网，为索，为珠。
Its kind becomes **feathers** (羽),
**stove** (灶),
**silk** (丝),
**net** (网),
**rope** (索),
and **pearl** (珠).

为文，为驳。
It becomes **patterns** (文) and **mixed colors** (驳).

为印，为绶，为书。
It becomes **seals** (印),
**ribbons** (绶),
and **writings** (书).

北方之奇为羽，南方之类为羽。
The **strange** (奇) of the **Northern Direction** (北方) is **feathers** (羽),
and the **kind** (类) of the **Southern Direction** (南方) is also **feathers** (羽).

吴天之气，以火蒸水，自北冲南，而羽象生焉。
The **qi of Heaven** (吴天之气) steams **water** (水) with **fire** (火),
rushing from the **North** (北) to the **South** (南),
giving rise to the **feather symbol** (羽象).

其养为灶，其杨为丝，其交为网，其纠为索，其凝清明为珠。
Its **nourishment** (养) is the **stove** (灶),
its **growth** (杨) is **silk** (丝),
its **interweaving** (交) is the **net** (网),
its **twisting** (纠) is the **rope** (索),
and its **congealing clarity** (凝清明) is the **pearl** (珠).

其变参错为文，驳者物相杂也。
Its **varied transformations** (变) interweave into **patterns** (文),
while **mixed colors** (驳) arise from **things intermingling** (物相杂).

皆象灶气上蒸。
All symbolize the **stove’s vapor rising** (灶气上蒸).

为印、绶、书，为文象定焉，
It becomes **seals** (印), **ribbons** (绶), and **writings** (书),
fixing the **pattern symbol** (文象).

凡此为羽之变也。
All these are **transformations of feathers** (羽之变).

为轻，为高，为台。
To become **lightness** (轻),
**height** (高),
and **platform** (台).

为酒，为吐，为射，为戈，为甲，为丛。
To become **alcohol** (酒),
**vomiting** (吐),
**arrows** (射),
**spears** (戈),
**armor** (甲),
and **clusters** (丛).

上炎之气，弗缊而发，则为轻，为高，为台。
When the **upper scorching qi** (上炎之气) **does not condense** (弗缊) but **emits** (发),
it becomes **lightness** (轻),
**height** (高),
and **platform** (台).

其缊而发，则为酒，为吐，为射，为戈，为甲，为丛。
When it **condenses and emits** (缊而发),
it becomes **alcohol** (酒),
**vomiting** (吐),
**arrows** (射),
**spears** (戈),
**armor** (甲),
and **clusters** (丛).

凡草木皆以火拔水，触土而生者也。
All **grasses and trees** (草木) **draw water with fire** (火拔水),
sprouting when they **touch earth** (触土).

为司马，为礼，为绳，为火工，为刀。
To become **Marshal** (司马),
**ritual** (礼),
**measuring line** (绳),
**fire artisan** (火工),
and **knife** (刀).

为射，为戈，为甲，为丛，此司马之所乘，以务烈也下。
To become **arrows** (射),
**spears** (戈),
**armor** (甲),
and **clusters** (丛)—
these are the **Marshal’s tools** (司马之所乘),
used to **pursue ferocity** (务烈) below.

武成履乱者，理焉，故为礼。
When **Martial Virtue** (武成) **steps into chaos** (履乱),
it **orders** (理) it,
thus becoming **ritual** (礼).

礼以约物，使从正直，故为绳。
**Ritual** (礼) **restrains things** (约物),
making them follow **rectitude** (正直),
thus becoming the **measuring line** (绳).

绳以人辅天而治之，故为火工。
The **measuring line** (绳) aids **humans in governing with Heaven** (人辅天),
thus becoming the **fire artisan** (火工).

戈，支兵也，象物萌芽。
The **spear** (戈) is the **branch of weaponry** (支兵),
symbolizing **things sprouting** (物萌芽).

而刀正火类，刀制义也。
The **knife** (刀) aligns with the **fire category** (火类),
as it **judges righteousness** (制义).

为赤怪，为盲，为舒。
To become **red anomaly** (赤怪),
**blindness** (盲),
and **relaxation** (舒).

赤怪，灾也。
**Red anomaly** (赤怪) is **calamity** (灾).

盲，丧其明。
**Blindness** (盲) is the **loss of clarity** (丧其明).

舒，豫咎也。
**Relaxation** (舒) is **premature doom** (豫咎).

一六为水，为北方，为冬。
**One six** (一六) becomes **Water** (水),
the **Northern Direction** (北方),
and **Winter** (冬).

日壬癸，辰子亥。
Days: **Ren** (壬) and **Gui** (癸),
Hours: **Chen** (辰), **Zi** (子), **Hai** (亥).

诸家作子亥，宋作亥子。
Some texts render it as **Zi Hai** (子亥),
while **Song** (宋) renders it as **Hai Zi** (亥子).

声羽，色黑，味咸，臭朽，形下。
Its **sound** (声) is **Yu** (羽),
**color** (色) is **black** (黑),
**taste** (味) is **salty** (咸),
**odor** (臭) is **rotten** (朽),
and its **form** (形) is **low** (下).

生木，胜火。
It **nourishes wood** (生木),
and **overcomes fire** (胜火).

时藏，藏肾，存精。
Its **season** (时) is **concealment** (藏),
it **stores in the kidneys** (藏肾),
and **preserves essence** (存精).

性智，情悲。
Its **nature** (性) is **wisdom** (智),
its **emotion** (情) is **sorrow** (悲).

事听，用聪。
Its **affairs** (事) are **hearing** (听),
its **utility** (用) is **acute perception** (聪).

撝谋，征寒。
Its **augury** (撝) is **planning** (谋),
its **auspice** (征) is **cold** (寒).

帝颛顼，神玄冥，星从其位。
Its **Emperor** (帝) is **Zhuānxū** (颛顼),
its **Deity** (神) is **Xuánmíng** (玄冥),
and its **stars** (星) follow their positions (从其位).

女、虚、危、室、壁，位亥子。
Stars: **Nǚ** (女), **Xū** (虚), **Wēi** (危), **Shì** (室), **Bì** (壁),
positioned at **Hai** (亥) and **Zi** (子).

类为介，为鬼，为祠，为庙。
Its kind becomes **shells** (介),
**ghosts** (鬼),
**shrines** (祠),
and **temples** (庙).

为井，为穴，为窦。
It becomes **wells** (井),
**caves** (穴),
and **holes** (窦).

为镜，为玉。
It becomes **mirrors** (镜)
and **jade** (玉).

陷乎险中，其象为介。
Falling into **peril** (险),
its symbol is the **shell** (介).

为鬼，为祠，为庙，以潜灵也。
To become **ghosts** (鬼),
**shrines** (祠),
and **temples** (庙)—
to **conceal spirits** (潜灵).

为井，为穴，为窦，以深通也。
To become **wells** (井),
**caves** (穴),
and **holes** (窦)—
to **achieve deep penetration** (深通).

为镜，以静明也。
To become **mirrors** (镜)—
to **achieve still clarity** (静明).

为玉，以洁清也。
To become **jade** (玉)—
to **achieve purity and clarity** (洁清).

皆水之在原者也。
All are **water in its primordial state** (水之在原).

为履，为远行，为劳，为血，为膏。
To become **footwear** (履),
**long journeys** (远行),
**toil** (劳),
**blood** (血),
and **fat** (膏).

其流为履，为远行，为劳，为血。
Its **flow** (流) becomes **footwear** (履),
**long journeys** (远行),
**toil** (劳),
and **blood** (血).

血凝其滋，而膏生焉，则物着而贪起矣。
When **blood** (血) **congeals its nourishment** (凝其滋),
**fat** (膏) arises,
and **things adhere**, giving rise to **greed** (贪).

为贪，为含，为蛰。
To become **greed** (贪),
**concealment** (含),
and **hibernation** (蛰).

为火猎，宋作人猎。
To become **fire hunting** (火猎),
though **Song** (宋) renders it as **human hunting** (人猎).

为闭，为盗。
To become **seclusion** (闭)
and **theft** (盗).

翕取为贪，怀藏为含。
**Gathering** (翕取) is **greed** (贪),
**hoarding** (怀藏) is **concealment** (含).

翕取生寒，怀藏至伏，是以为蛰。
**Gathering** (翕取) breeds **cold** (生寒),
**hoarding** (怀藏) reaches **hiding** (至伏),
thus becoming **hibernation** (蛰).

於物为蛰。
In **things**, it is **hibernation** (蛰).

为火猎，救人。
To become **fire hunting** (火猎)—
to **rescue people** (救人).

为闭，为盗，在险象也。
To become **seclusion** (闭)
and **theft** (盗)—
symbolizing **peril** (在险象).

含有畏

「It is **rigid yet timely in killing** (刚而时杀),
so its **emotion** (情) is **anger** (怒).

**Rites** (礼) and **things** (物) gather in **auspicious meetings** (嘉会相见),
so its **emotion** (情) is **joy** (乐).

**Wisdom** (智) stands alone, not merging with **things** (物),
yet **endlessly rescues** (善救不已),
so its **emotion** (情) is **sorrow** (悲).

The *Book of Documents* (《书》) says:
*"The human heart is ever perilous (人心惟危),
the Dao-heart ever subtle (道心惟微).
Only the refined, the singular (惟精惟一),
can steadfastly uphold the middle (允执厥中).
When the middle is not lost (中不失),
then it is the means to **settle peril** (定危).
When the middle shifts (中动),
it becomes the **emotion of fear** (恐惧之情)—
as when **Earth** (二五) is **overthrown** (震), this is already so."*

When the **heart** (心) is **shaken by things** (震于物)
and lacks steadfastness (无守则者),
it is not the **true nature of emotion** (情之正).

**Contemplation** (事思) and **enlightenment** (用睿),
**assisting the Sage** (撝圣),
**harnessing the winds** (征风)—

**Emperor** (帝) **Yellow** (黄) **the Yellow** (帝),
**Divine Sovereign** (神) **Hou** (后) **Tu** (土),
**Stars** (星) follow their **positions** (从其位).

**Jiao** (角) and **Kang** (亢) are positioned at **Chen** (辰),
**Kui** (奎) and **Lou** (娄) at **Xu** (戌),
**Dou** (斗) and **Niu** (牛) at **Chou** (丑),
**Jing** (井) and **Gui** (鬼) at **Wei** (未).

It is akin to **nakedness** (裸),
**sealing** (封),
though **Song** (宋) renders it as **sealing** (封)
and **mounds** (垄).

It is like a **vessel** (瓶).

It is a **palace** (宫),
a **residence** (宅),
a **central channel** (中溜).

It is **internal affairs** (内事),
**weaving** (织),
**clothing** (衣),
**garments** (裘).

It is **cocoons** (茧),
**down** (絮).

It is **beds** (床),
**mattresses** (荐).

**Nakedness** (裸) lacks scales, feathers, or fur—
the **body** (体) is **central** (中) and **bare** (而已).

The **Divine** (神) has no fixed form,
and the **Dao** (道) has not yet begun to **seal** (封).
Once **sealed** (封已),
this **boundary** (疆) and **territory** (界) arise.

Once **sealed** (封已),
it is like a **vessel** (瓶)—no more.

A **vessel** (瓶) **congeals Earth** (凝土) to become an **instrument** (器);
a **palace** (宫) **excavates Earth** (凿土) to become a **chamber** (室).

A **residence** (宅) is where one **dwells** (居).
Between the **palace** (宫) and **residence** (宅),
the **central channel** (中溜),
there are **internal affairs** (内事).

**Earth** (土) accumulates **yin** (阴),
and its **work** (功) completes **things** (作成物),
**discerning patterns** (识法) and **weft and warp** (经纬),
to make **clothing** (衣) and **garments** (裘)—
all **internal affairs** (内事).

**Nakedness** (裸) **contemplates** (思) how to **warm itself** (所以自燠),
thus **cocoons** (茧) **seal themselves** (自封),
mirroring the **human heart for clothing** (人衣裘之心).

**Hiding** (藏) within **clothing** (衣裘)
yet still **insufficient** (不足),
it **seeks** (因) **cocoons** (茧) and **down** (絮).

It **creates its own central channel** (自为中溜),
using **emptiness** (虚) and **transformation** (变) to **communicate** (通),
**benefiting life** (利用生).

To **beds** (床) and **mattresses** (荐),
it **settles its true nature** (宁厥正),
the **ultimate of stability** (安厚之极).

It is **domestication** (驯),
**embracing** (怀),
**abdominal organs** (腹器).

It is **fat** (脂),
**lacquer** (漆),
**glue** (胶).

It is **bags** (囊),
**wrappings** (包).

**Domestication** (驯) is the **way of women** (妇道).
**Embracing** (怀) is the **way of mothers** (母道).
With **embracing** (怀),
it becomes **abdominal organs** (腹器).

The **congealing of moderation** (中和之凝)
is **fat** (脂),
**lacquer** (漆),
**glue** (胶).

When **preserved and combined** (保合),
it becomes **bags** (囊) and **wrappings** (包).
This is how the **way of mothers** (母道) **completes things** (成物).

It is **chariots** (舆),
**axles** (毂).

It is **cultivation** (稼),
**parsimony** (啬).

It is **food** (食),
**sharing** (与).

It is **coffins** (棺),
**lids** (椟), though **Song** (宋) renders it as **coffin** (椁).

It is **crossroads** (衢),
**gatherings** (会),
**metropolises** (都).

It is **measurement** (度),
**scale** (量).

It is **earthworks** (土工),
**bows and arrows** (弓矢).

**Chariots** (舆) **carry** (载) with **rectitude** (方),
**axles** (毂) **operate centrally** (中运).

It is **cultivation** (稼),
**parsimony** (啬).

It is **food** (食),
**giving** (与).

It is **coffins** (棺),
**lids** (椟), symbolizing **Earth’s bearing and movement** (象地载之运).

The *Book of Documents* (《书》) says:
*"Earth **cultivates** (爰稼) **grain and harvests** (穑).*
**Food** (食) **realizes itself** (以自实),
and **nourishes life** (腴其生),
thus **death** (死) arises.
**Coffins** (棺) are what **humans return to Earth** (人之所以及於土) with.

All **hundreds of transformations** (百昌) **emerge from Earth** (生於土),
and **return to Earth** (反於土),
so that **life’s return to its origin** (生之生於本) is like **lids** (椟).

**Life and death** (死生) **cycle endlessly** (往复),
like **crossroads** (衢).
**Crossroads** (衢) are **pathways of convergence** (会通).

Four **directions** (达) converge,
and the **center** (中) is their **metropolis** (都).
**Measurement** (度) and **scale** (量) are **meticulously applied** (法谨),
and **earthworks** (土工) **depend on it** (资之).

**Governance** (治) of a **state** (国) reaches **bows and arrows** (弓矢)—
this is the **ultimate** (极).

Thus it is said:
*"The **movement of the Five Weapons** (五兵之运) is the **end of virtue** (德之末)."*

The **sprouting of things** (物之萌生),
**separating from concealment** (离潜),
**emerging and hiding** (发伏),
is like the **arrows of a bow** (弓之矢),
the **string of a bow** (弓之彀),
**wandering through the center** (率游於中央).

It is akin to **yellow monstrosities** (黄怪),
**foolishness** (愚),
**dazzling blindness** (牟).
**Song** (宋) says **dazzling blindness** (牟) should be **blindness** (瞀).

**Evil** (妖) does not **arise on its own** (不自兴),
it comes from **humans reversing virtue** (由人反德).

**Foolishness** (愚) is a **disease of the heart** (心之疾).
**Dazzling blindness** (牟) is **interchangeable with confusion** (与蒙通),
a **fault of muddled impurity** (零浊之咎).

The **mysterious calculations** (玄数) of the **Five Phases** (五行)
**illuminate** (昭) the **patterns of things** (事类),
thus the *Great Treatise of the Yellow River* (《洪范》) **orders the Five Phases** (五行为序).

**Deeply knowing** (深知) the **Five Phases** (五行)
allows one to **discuss the Dao** (论道),
to **establish rites** (制礼)—
not merely to **revere their divinations** (特尚其占).

When the **Five Phases** (五行) **take effect** (用事), **kingship** (王) arises,
and **kingship** (王) **generates mutual relations** (所生相).
Thus when **kingship** (王) **declines** (废),
the **one who overcomes kingship** (胜王) **is imprisoned** (囚),
and the **one kingship overcomes** (王所胜) **dies** (死).

In **sound** (声),
**Gong** (宫) is the **Sovereign** (君),
**Zheng** (征) is **affairs** (事),
**Shang** (商) is the **minister** (相),
**Jue** (角) is the **people** (民),
**Yu** (羽) is **things** (物).

In **music** (律吕),
**Yellow Bell** (黄钟) **generates** (生) **Forest Bell** (林钟),
**Forest Bell** (林钟) **generates** (生) **Grand Subduing** (太簇),
**Grand Subduing** (太簇) **generates** (生) **Southern Reeds** (南吕),
**Southern Reeds** (南吕) **generates** (生) **Maoshi** (姑洗),
**Maoshi** (姑洗) **generates** (生) **Responding Bell** (应钟),
**Responding Bell** (应钟) **generates** (生) **Rui Bin** (蕤宾),
**Rui Bin** (蕤宾) **generates** (生) **Great Reeds** (大吕),
**Great Reeds** (大吕) **generates** (生) **Equable** (夷则),
**Equable** (夷则) **generates** (生) **Intermediate Bell** (夹钟),
**Intermediate Bell** (夹钟) **generates** (生) **None Shooting** (无射),
**None Shooting** (无射) **generates** (生) **Central Reeds** (仲吕).

**Affairs** (事) **transform and converge** (变通),
**ministers** (相) **govern and regulate** (宰制),
**people** (民) **are born and harmonized** (生而和),
**things** (物) **are hidden and transformed** (藏而化).

The **Sovereign** (君) **remains central without action** (中心无为),
to **guard the utmost rectitude** (守至正),
so all **sounds** (凡声),
**heavy** (重) do not **exceed Gong** (不逾宫),
and **light** (轻) do not **fall below Yu** (不过羽).

**Eighty-one** (九九八十一) is **Gong** (宫),
**three parts minus one** (三分去一) is **Fifty-four** (五十四) for **Zheng** (征);
**three parts plus one** (三分益一) is **Seventy-two** (七十二) for **Shang** (商);
**three parts minus one** (三分去一) is **Forty-eight** (四十八) for **Yu** (羽);
**three parts plus one** (三分益一) is **Sixty-four** (六十四) for **Jue** (角).

This is the **Yellow Bell’s** (黄钟) **method of balancing the Five Sounds** (均五声法).

The **Twelve Pitches** (十二律) each **adopt their own numbers** (各以其数) as **Gong** (宫),
and **reduce or augment** (损益) to **generate Zheng, Shang, Yu, Jue** (生征、商、羽、角),
thus **completing sixty sounds** (为六十声).

The **Yellow Bell’s** (黄钟) **tube** (管) is **nine inches** (九寸),
**three parts minus one** (三分去一) **produces Forest Bell** (下生林钟);
The **Forest Bell’s** (林钟) **tube** (管) is **six inches** (六寸),
**three parts plus one** (三分益一) **produces Grand Subduing** (上生太簇);
The **Grand Subduing’s** (太簇) **tube** (管) is **eight inches** (八寸),
**three parts minus one** (三分去一) **produces Southern Reeds** (下生南吕), **five inches and one-third** (五寸三分寸之一);
The **Southern Reeds** (南吕) **generate Maoshi** (上生姑洗), **seven inches and nine-tenths** (七寸九分寸之一);
The **Maoshi** (姑洗) **generate Responding Bell** (下生应钟), **four inches and twenty-seven-hundredths** (四寸二十七分寸之二十);
The **Responding Bell** (应钟) **generate Rui Bin** (上生蕤宾), **six inches and eighty-one-hundredths** (六寸八十一分寸之二十六);
The **Rui Bin** (蕤宾) **generate Great Reeds** (又上生大吕), **eight inches and two hundred forty-three-hundredths** (八寸二百四十三分寸之百四);
The **Great Reeds** (大吕) **generate Equable** (下生夷则), **five inches and seven hundred twenty-nine-hundredths** (五寸七百二十九分寸之四百五十一);

The **Equable** (夷则) **generates Intercalary Bell** (夹钟), **seven inches and two thousand one hundred eighty-seven-hundredths** (七寸二千一百八十七分寸之千七十五);

The **Intercalary Bell** (夹钟) **generates Unshot** (无射), **four inches and six thousand five hundred sixty-one-hundredths** (四寸六千五百六十一分寸之六千五百二十四);

The **Unshot** (无射) **generates Middle Reeds** (中吕), **six inches and ten thousand nine hundred sixty-three-hundredths** (六寸万九千六百八十三分寸之万二千九百七十四).

For indeed, the numbers of **augmentation and diminution** (损益) do not exceed **three**, and the numbers of **generation and derivation** (生取) do not exceed **eight**.

Thus, it **harmonizes the two extremes** (统和二极) and **narrates the eight winds** (述行八风).

From **Zi** (子) to **Si** (巳) are all **yang cycles** (阳纪);
**Great Reeds** (大吕), **Intercalary Bell** (夹钟), and **Middle Reeds** (中吕) are the **yin tones within yang** (阳中之阴声).

From **Wu** (午) to **Hai** (亥) are all **yin cycles** (阴纪);
**Rui Bin** (蕤宾), **Southern Reeds** (南吕), and **Responding Bell** (应钟) are the **yang tones within yin** (阴中之阳声).

Thus, from **Zi** to **Si**, all are **generated downward** (下生);
From **Wu** to **Hai**, all are **generated upward** (上生).

In music, if **Huangzhong** (黄钟) is the **gong** (宫), then **Linzhong** (林钟) is the **zheng** (征), **Taicuo** (太簇) is the **shang** (商), **Nanlu** (南吕) is the **yu** (羽), and **Goushi** (姑洗) is the **jiao** (角);

If **Linzhong** (林钟) is the **gong** (宫), then **Taicuo** (太簇) is the **zheng** (征), **Nanlu** (南吕) is the **shang** (商), **Goushi** (姑洗) is the **yu** (羽), and **Yingzhong** (应钟) is the **jiao** (角);

If **Taicuo** (太簇) is the **gong** (宫), then **Nanlu** (南吕) is the **zheng** (征), **Goushi** (姑洗) is the **shang** (商), **Yingzhong** (应钟) is the **yu** (羽), and **Ruibin** (蕤宾) is the **jiao** (角).

In all, the **five tones** (五声) and **six lü twelve pipes** (六律十二管) **cyclically become the gong** (旋相为宫).

By **three transformations** (三变通), this is what is recorded as **"spreading the Five Phases across the Four Seasons, harmonizing to then give birth to the months"** (播五行於四时，和而后月生).

The **Five Phases** (五行) **alternately reign** (更王用事), one **rectifies and conquers** (一正胜), and **harmonizes with generation** (而参以生和), this is what the *Yijing* calls **"the nature and disposition of what is beneficial and upright"** (利贞之性情).

The numbers of **Zi and Wu** (子午) are **nine**, **Chou and Wei** (丑未) are **eight**, **Yin and Shen** (寅申) are **seven**, **Mao and You** (卯酉) are **six**, **Chen and Xu** (辰戌) are **five**, **Si and Hai** (巳亥) are **four**.

Thus, there are **forty-two lü** (律四十二), and **thirty-six lü** (吕三十六).

Combining the numbers of **lü and lü**, some **return** (或还) and some **do not** (或否), totaling **seventy-eight** (凡七十有八), and the number of **Huangzhong** (黄钟) is established.

All these are **derived from Huangzhong** (皆生黄钟).

**Zi and Wu** (子午) are the **Celestial and Earthly** means of **establishing the Supreme Pole** (天地之所以经皇极), and the number **nine** (九数) is **fulfilled** (缊焉).

Yet their **decline reaches Si and Hai** (杀至于巳亥), and the **lü** (律) **integrates the numbers of Zi, Wu, Yin, Shen, Chen, and Xu** (综子午寅申辰戌之数) to make **forty-two**, while the **lü** (吕) **integrates the numbers of Chou, Wei, Mao, You, Si, and Hai** (综丑未卯酉巳亥之数) to make **thirty-six**.

Combined, they total **seventy-eight** (凡七十有八).

Yet the numbers of **lü and lü**, **Huangzhong alone returns to nine** (黄钟独还得九), while the others do not.

Thus, **Huangzhong is the master of lü and lü** (黄钟为律吕之宗).

The number of **Huangzhong** is **eighty-one** (黄钟之数八十有一), yet it is **established at seventy-eight** (而立於七十有八).

Thus, **three are left void** (虚其三), as the **mystery of all wonders** (以为众妙之玄).

The reason for using **nine** (所以用九者也) is to **triple three** (参三焉), and the **twelve zodiacal branches** (十有二辰) stop at **four**, thus **establishing the square** (则以立方而已矣).

All these **measurements derive from Huangzhong** (皆由黄钟者).

From the **breadth of ninety grains** (九十黍之广) **length is generated**, and from the **pipe of nine inches** (九寸之管) **measure is generated**.

From its **weight of one thousand two hundred grains** (一千二百黍之重) as **twelve zhu** (十二铢), **weights and measures are generated** (而生权衡也).

The numbers of **Jia and Si** (甲巳) are **nine**#1, **Yi and Geng** (乙庚) are **eight**, **Bing and Xin** (丙辛) are **seven**, **Ding and Ren** (丁壬) are **six**, **Wu and Gui** (戊癸) are **five**.

**Tones are generated from the days** (声生於日), **lü from the zodiacal branches** (律生於辰).

**Tones are straight by nature and quality** (声以情质), **lü are narrated by harmony and sound** (律以和声).

When **tone and lü accord**, the **eight kinds of sound are born** (声律相协，而八音生).

The **Celestial numbers are five**, the **Earthly numbers are five**, and the **five positions** (五位) **mutually attain harmony**, each having its **resonance** (各有合), thus the **ten days** (十日) are as such.

**Celestial and Earthly sincerity** (天地中孚) is **manifested in Jiazi** (象见甲子).

**Jia** is the **first origin** (一元也).

One becomes **three**, three becomes **nine**, and the numbers are **exhausted** (而数究焉).

Thus, the number of **Jia** is **nine**, and the number of **Ji** is also **nine**#2, following their **harmony** (从其合也).

The number of **Jia** is **nine**, descending to **Yi**, **Bing**, **Ding**, and **Wu**;

The number of **Ji** is **nine**#3, descending to **Geng**, **Xin**, **Ren**, and **Gui**.

The numbers **reach their limit at five**, thus the **days govern by their cycles** (是故日以冲运也).

**Jia and Yi** (甲乙) are **jiao** (角), **Bing and Ding** (丙丁) are **zheng** (征), **Geng and Xin** (庚辛) are **shang** (商), **Ren and Gui** (壬癸) are **yu** (羽), **Wu and Ji** (戊己) are **gong** (宫)#4.

Thus, **tones are generated from the days** (声生於日), the **qi of Heaven** (天之气);

**Lü are generated from the zodiacal branches** (律生於辰), the **law of Earth** (地之法).

**Tones are rectified by nature and quality** (声直之以情质), **lü are narrated by harmony and sound** (律述之以和声).

Thus, the sounds of **metal, stone, silk, bamboo, gourd, leather, and wood** (金石丝竹匏土革木) are born, and **tone can be harmonized to form culture** (声可和而成文).

This is because **each day has its resonance** (凡以日各有合故也).

The **Nine Heavens** (九天):
One is **Central Heaven** (中天), two is **Excess Heaven** (羡天), three is **Following Heaven** (从天), four is **Changing Heaven** (更天), five is **Blinking Heaven** (睟天), six is **Boundless Heaven** (廓天), seven is **Reduced Heaven** (减天), eight is **Sunken Heaven** (沈天), nine is **Completed Heaven** (成天).

The **Nine Earths** (九地):
One is **sandy mud** (沙泥), two is **marshes and pools** (泽池), three is **shallow cliffs** (沚崖), four is **lower fields** (下田), five is **middle fields** (中田), six is **upper fields** (上田), seven is **lower mountains** (下山), eight is **middle mountains** (中山), nine is **upper mountains** (上山).

The **Nine People** (九人):
One is **lowly person** (下人), two is **common person** (平人), three is **ascending person** (进人), four is **low fortune** (下禄), five is **middle fortune** (中禄), six is **high fortune** (上禄), seven is **lost aspiration** (失志), eight is **sick and stagnant** (疾淤), **Song reads as stagnant-sick** (宋作淤疾), nine is **extreme** (极).

The **Nine Movements** (九行) are by **action**, according to **beginning, middle, and end** (据始、中、终);

The **Nine Earths** are by **position**, according to **lower, middle, and upper** (据下、中、上);

The **Nine People** are by **observation of motion**, according to **thought, fortune, and calamity** (据思、福、祸).

The **Nine Bodies** (九体):
One is **hands and feet** (手足), two is **arms and legs** (臂胫), three is **thighs and arms** (股肱), four is **vital points** (要), five is **abdomen** (腹), six is **shoulders** (肩), seven is **[missing/obscure]** (，，，，音呀); **[*Zhushu Jijie* reads as *kū*, Song reads as *hú*]** (，《释文》音枯，宋音胡), eight is **face** (面), nine is **forehead** (颡).

The **Nine Affinities** (九属):
One is **great-grandchild** (玄孙), two is **great-great-grandchild** (曾孙), three is **great-great-great-grandchild** (仍孙), four is **child** (子), five is **self** (身), six is **father** (父), seven is **grandfather** (祖父), eight is **great-grandfather** (曾祖父), nine is **highest ancestor** (高祖父).

The **Nine Orifices** (九窍):
One and six are **front** (前), **ears** (耳);
Two and seven are **eyes** (目);
Three and eight are **nose** (鼻);
Four and nine are **mouth** (口);
Five and five are **back** (后).

The **Nine Manifestations** (九体) and **Nine Affinities** (九属) reveal the count of solar terms (日辰之数). The descending sequence from the **Nine Differences** (九差) is indeed the natural order.

The **Nine Sequences** (九序):
One is **First of First** (孟孟),
Two is **First of Middle** (孟仲),
Three is **First of Last** (孟季),
Four is **Middle of First** (仲孟),
Five is **Middle of Middle** (仲仲),
Six is **Middle of Last** (仲季),
Seven is **Last of First** (季孟),
Eight is **Last of Middle** (季仲),
Nine is **Last of Last** (季季).

The **Nine Matters** (九事):
One is **Establishing Framework** (规模),
Two is **Rectification and Obstruction** (方沮),
Three is **Natural Adaptation** (自如),
Four is **External Diversion** (外它),
Five is **Internal Harmony** (中和),
Six is **Abundance and Excess** (盛多),
Seven is **Decline** (消),
Eight is **Exhaustion** (耗),
Nine is **Final Defect** (尽弊).

The **Nine Years** (九年):
One is **ten years** (一十),
Two is **twenty years** (二十),
Three is **thirty years** (三十),
Four is **forty years** (四十),
Five is **fifty years** (五十),
Six is **sixty years** (六十),
Seven is **seventy years** (七十),
Eight is **eighty years** (八十),
Nine is **ninety years** (九十).

The **Nine Affinities** govern the **Nine Manifestations** and **Nine Orifices** (九窍), for the **Manifestations** and **Orifices** are the foundation upon which human **Affinities** are established. The **Nine Matters** govern the **Nine Sequences** and **Nine Years**, for the **Sequences** and **Years** are the means by which human **Matters** are conducted.

The **Sequences** advance in cycles of three years, completing ten.

The **Mysterious Calculations** (玄算) for divination:
**Family** (家), one is placed as one, two as two, three as three;
**Division** (部), one does not increase, two increase by three, three increase by six;
**State** (州), one does not increase, two increase by nine, three increase by eighteen;
**Direction** (方), one does not increase, two increase by twenty-seven, three increase by fifty-four.

*The Law of Speech (法言)* states:
*The Book of Changes (易)*, a work of numbers, can be counted. What can be counted is also what is complete. The *Book of Documents (书)* lacks more than half its content, yet scholars unfamiliar with it cannot grasp its essence, for there are no numerical principles to establish its categories and forms. The **Mysterious Calculations** allow the diviner to know the order of the **First Praises** (首赞) concerning the day and stars, thus maintaining the celestial order (经天) and human relationships (彝伦) without confusion.

If one obtains a **Direction**, a **State**, a **Division**, and three **Families** in divination, then the **Family** is placed as three, and the **Direction**, **State**, and **Division** are all without increase, totaling three. This is the order of the **First Praise** (玄首之次), three in count. All increases are derived from the initial **Family** numbers.

To seek the **Praise of Manifestation** (表之赞), place the **Mysterious Name** (玄姓), subtract the **Great Beginning** (太始) divination count, reduce by one and multiply by nine, then add the **Praise**. Subtract half of the **Mysterious Name** count, and one obtains the **Praise** subtracted from the Winter Solstice count.

Even is the night of the obtained day, odd is the day of the obtained day. Xu (许) and Huang (黄) read this as *ming* (明), Song (宋) and Guo (郭) read it as *dé* (得).

Placing the **Mysterious Name** (玄姓), subtracting the **Great Beginning** count and reducing by one means subtracting the first **Praise** of the placed **Mysterious Name**. Multiplying by nine means each **Praise** is counted nine times. Subtracting the first **Praise** of the **Mysterious Name**, one then calculates the **Praise** to be added. One **Praise** increases by one, two by two, three by three.

To seek the day, subtract the **Mysterious Name** count from the **Praise**, then halve it: two **Praises** make one day, hence an even **Praise** is the night, and an odd **Praise** is the day.

If divination yields a response, from the center to the response, totaling forty-one, then place forty-one, reduce by one and multiply by nine, resulting in three hundred sixty. Add the obtained **Praise**, subtract half of three hundred sixty, and one obtains one hundred eighty, which is the count subtracted from the Winter Solstice.

Increase by one to get three hundred sixty-one, an odd **Praise**, marking the one hundred eighty-one days of the day. Increase by two to get three hundred sixty-two, an even **Praise**, marking the one hundred eighty-one days of the night.

To seek the star, begin with **The Ox of the Net** (牵牛). When the **Mysterious Calculations** are exhausted, that is the day. From the Winter Solstice, **The Ox of the Net** moves one degree per day, completing one degree per day.

Thus, when the star degrees are exhausted, one obtains the degree where the day resides.

End of *The Great Mysterious Calculations* (太玄数) Volume Eight.
#1 Original text: 『己』 changed to 『乙』 according to Fan’s edition.
#2#3#4 Original text: 『己』 changed to 『巳』 according to the correct Heavenly Stems (天干) in the main text.
*Great Mysterious Calculations* (太玄文) Volume Nine, *Mysterious Calculations* (玄文).

The **Vague**, the **Direct**, the **Covered**, the **Mature**, and the **Dark**. The **Vague** is the north, winter, where form has not yet emerged. The **Direct** is the east, spring, where substance exists but lacks adornment. The **Covered** is the south, summer, where things grow long and may all be grasped and worn. *Xu* and *Huang* read it as **Load** (载), *Zhang* and *Ding* as **Wear** (戴), *Guo* as **Wear** (戴).

The **Mature** is the west, autumn, where all things take shape and are completed. When form exists, it returns to the formless, hence the **Dark**. Therefore, all things are **Vague** in the north, **Direct** in the east, **Covered** in the south, **Mature** in the west, and **Dark** in the north.

Thus, the **Vague** is the dwelling of the **Having**; the **Direct**, the foundation of **Adornment**; the **Covered**, the master of **Decay**; the **Mature**, the repository of **Life**; and the **Dark**, the storehouse of **Illumination**.

The **Vague** shelters its **Qi**; the **Direct** encounters its kind. The **Covered** reaches its peak in growth; the **Mature** examines its completion. *Fan* notes: "Examine things to make them fully realized." The main text reads **Close** (亲), but this is an error by the copyist. *Song* and *Guo* read it as **Completion** (就). The **Dark** reflects its depths.

The **Vague** and **Covered** reach extremes; the **Direct** and **Mature** admonish each other. Emerging from the **Dark** and returning to the **Dark**, the new and the old alternate. *Zhang* reads it as **Loan** (贷).

Yin and Yang succeed one another; clarity and turbidity intermingle. Those who advance are promoted; those who succeed are retired. When used, they are **debased**; when timely, they are **noble**. The celestial patterns and earthly substances remain unaltered in their positions.

The **Vague**, the **Direct**, the **Covered**, the **Mature**, and the **Dark**. From the **Vague** come speech, action, and blessings or calamities. In the **Vague**’s time, all is mysterious indeed.

Action leaves a trace; speech has sound; blessings bring **Strength** (膊). *Yin* **Shàn** (剸) means "to cut flesh"; also read as *Yin* **Shùnguǎn** (竖衮). Calamities manifest in form—this is the **Direct**.

If there is the **Direct**, one may be **Covered**; if **Covered**, one may reach **Maturity**; if **Mature**, one returns to the **Dark**. Therefore, in the **Vague**’s time, all may be regulated—thus the eighty-one schools arise from the **Vague**.

The heavens shine brilliantly from the **boundless** (无畛). *Yin* **Xuàn** (炫) is read as *Hu* **Yàn** (胡绚). The **radiant** (熿熿) emerges from the **limitless** (无垠). *Yin* **Guāng** (熿) is read as *Hù* **Guāng** (户光), the same as **Resplendent** (煌).

Thus, in the **Vague**’s time, all is mysterious indeed. Therefore, the Dao of Heaven conceals itself in **depth**, stirs to **reveal**, exalts to **overlook**, regulates to **restrain**, and concludes in **obscurity**. Its depths are unfathomable; its brilliance is boundless.

Hence, the sage hides in **depth** to properly honor the spirits, stirs to **reveal** to inspire the people, shines brightly to **encompass** and illuminate, regulates to **restrain** to make all tremble—*Yin* **Nǐlì** (牛力) or *Yin* **Nǐ** (拟)—and conceals in **obscurity** to remain hidden.

The sage who embodies these five aspects is thus called the **Vague**, the **Direct**, the **Covered**, the **Mature**, and the **Dark**.

Someone asks: Why does *Kunlun* **Pāngbó** (昆仑旁薄) relate to **obscurity** (幽)?

It is said: The sage, like the heavens and earth, contemplates and encompasses all things. Within *Kunlun*, form has not yet manifested externally; dwelling alone in joy, pondering alone in sorrow—joy is unbearable, sorrow is insurmountable—hence it is called **obscurity**.

Why does the spirit contend in the **mysterious** (玄)?

It is said: The petty person’s heart is mixed, seeking to manifest externally, and uses Yin and Yang to contend over auspiciousness or inauspiciousness. Yang contends over auspiciousness; Yin contends over inauspiciousness.

The wind reveals the tiger; the clouds reveal the dragon. The sage acts, and all things harmonize. The dragon emerges from within—why is this so?

It is said: The dragon is where **virtue/power** (德) first takes form. If Yin does not reach its extreme, Yang does not arise; if chaos does not reach its extreme, **virtue/power** (德) does not manifest.

The sage cultivates **virtue/power** (德) to await the time, neither acting before its due nor lagging behind. When movement and stillness are subtly discerned, without losing their principles—who but the sage can do this?

Thus, the beginning and end may be used as **ordinary** (庸).

The *Kù* is empty with no cause—greatly receiving life and fate—why is this so?

It is said: The petty person cannot embrace emptiness or dwell in lowliness; they are **level and common** (庳), yet cannot be **overlooked**. Empty yet able to be **filled**, lacking yet able to **have**, relying on causes to **act**—thus they greatly receive life and fate without **avoidance** (辟), hence the *Kù* is **obscured** (否). All versions read it as "without **speech or avoidance** (无辞辟)," but *Ding* and *Zhang* omit the **speech** (无辞) character.

The day aligns with the heavens—why is this so?

The Sage rides in station,
as chariot and as steed—
the chariot’s **rim** (*lǎn*)[^1] and the horse’s **tail-hair knot** (*jiè*)[^2]
can traverse the world—
thus it is advantageous to be the **master**.

The moon withholds its embrace,
yet shines brighter in the West—
why is this so?

It is said: The petty person is **full and overflowing**.
Those who **self-destroy** from emptiness—
water **fades** into the depths,
trees **wither** to their roots,
mountains **wither** and grow lean,
marshes **swell** with fat.
The **virtuous** perceive this, yet the multitude knows not.

Why does the **head** (*qiú*)[^3] **enclose** the **true** (*zhēn*)?
It is said: **Ren** (*rén*) abhors **non-ren**,
**proper conduct** (*yì*) abhors **non-conduct**.
The Sage’s **generosity** suffices to **nourish the many**,
his **harmony and softness** suffice to **settle all things**.
Heaven and Earth contain all things—
what cannot be contained by Heaven and Earth
is only the **un-ren** and **un-conduct**.

Thus, water **encloses the true**.

Yellow not yellow—
why is this so?

It is said: The petty person **loses the central norm**.
All **ones** mark the **beginning**—
all **ones**, *Zhang* reads as **"say"** (*wèi*).
All **threes** mark the **end**—
the **two** obtain the **middle**?[^4]

The **virtuous** in **mystery** (*xuán*) are **upright** (*zhèng*), in **fortune** (*fú*) are **effusive** (*chōng*), in **calamity** (*huò*) are **resolute** (*fǎn*).
The petty in **mystery** are **deviant** (*yé*), in **fortune** are **arrogant** (*jiāo*), in **calamity** are **desperate** (*qióng*).

Thus, the **virtuous** in proper station **thrive** (*chāng*), in improper station remain **good** (*liáng*).
The petty in proper station **flourish** (*héng*), in improper station **perish** (*sàng*).
Even the **Eight** (*bā*—the Eight Trigrams) though in proper station,
still **revert** (*fù*) to the **constant** (*cháng*)—how is this so?

**Preternatural** (*diān*) **spirits** (*líng*), their **qi-forms** (*qìxíng*) **inverted** (*fǎn*), why is this so?
It is said: They are **severed** (*jué*) and **extreme** (*jí*) in the **upper** (*shàng*).
**Extreme** in the **upper** then **transforms** (*yùn*), severed in the **lower** (*xià*) **brings about reversal** (*diān*).

The **spirits** already **reversed** (*diān*), how can their **qi-forms** (*qìxíng*) **remain** (*zài*) without **inversion** (*fǎn*)?

The **virtuous** are those who reach **high age** (*gāo*) and **extreme times** (*jí shí*).

The **yang** is **extreme** in the **upper**, the **yin** is **extreme** in the **lower**.
**Qi-forms** (*qìxíng*) **err** (*kuàng*), **spirits** (*guǐ*) and **gods** (*shén*) **obstruct** (*zǔ*).
The **accomplished** (*xián*) **fear**, the petty **rely** (*hù*).

**Kunlun** (*kūnlún*) **flanks** (*páng*) **thinness** (*bó*), **excessive** (*tài*) **tolerance** (*róng*).
**Divine** (*shén*) **combat** (*zhàn*) in **mystery** (*xuán*), **mutual assault** (*xiāng gōng*).
The **Dragon** (*lóng*) **emerges** (*chū*) from the **center** (*zhōng*), **following** (*shì*) **its course** (*cóng*).

**Hollow** (*qū*) **emptiness** (*xū*) **denies** (*pǐ*), **unfairness** (*bù gōng*).
The **Sun** (*rì*) **aligns** (*zhèng*) in the **Heaven** (*tiān*), **radiance** (*guāng*) **penetrates** (*tōng*).
The **Moon** (*yuè*) **lacks** (*quē*) its **clasp** (*bó*), **waxing and waning** (*shǔn yíng*).
The **head** (*qiú*) **encloses** (*bāo*) the **true** (*zhēn*), **conforming** (*fǎ*) to the **virtue** (*dé*).

Yellow not yellow—
**losing** (*shī*) the **central norm** (*zhōng jīng*).
**Preternatural** (*diān*) **spirits** (*líng*) **inversion** (*fǎn*), **exhausting** (*qióng*) the **Heavenly** (*tiān*) **sentiment** (*qíng*).
**Mountain** (*gāng*) **erect** (*zhí*) **veiled** (*méng*) by the **head** (*qiú*), **praising** (*zàn*) the **group** (*qún*) in **darkness** (*míng*).
**Kunlun** (*kūnlún*) **flanks** (*páng*) **thinness** (*bó*), **resources** (*zī*) **and** (*huái*) **heart** (*wéi*) **lack direction** (*wú fāng*).
**Divine** (*shén*) **combat** (*zhàn*) in **mystery** (*xuán*), **deviance** (*yé*) and **uprightness** (*zhèng*) both **proceed** (*xíng*).
The **Dragon** (*lóng*) **emerges** (*chū*) from the **center** (*zhōng*), **law** (*fǎ*) and **degree** (*dù*) **cultivated** (*wén míng*).
**Hollow** (*qū*) **emptiness** (*xū*) **denies** (*pǐ*), **ministerial conduct** (*chén dào*) **improper** (*bù dāng*).
The **Sun** (*rì*) **aligns** (*zhèng*) in the **Heaven** (*tiān*), **riding** (*chéng*) the **unyielding** (*jiàng*) **of** (*zhī*) **Heaven** (*qián*).
The **Moon** (*yuè*) **lacks** (*quē*) its **clasp** (*bó*), **to observe** (*guàn*) **eclipse and return** (*xiāo shì*).
The **head** (*qiú*) **encloses** (*bāo*) the **true** (*zhēn*), **able** (*néng*) **to bear** (*rèn*) **punishment** (*xíng*) and **virtue** (*dé*).

**Able** (*néng*) **to bear** (*rèn*), **original** (*běn*) **capacity** (*néng*) **as** (*zuò*) **scrape** (*kāi*)—
*Zhang* reads as **"scrape"** (*kāi*), lacking the **able** (*néng*) character.
All **originals** (*zhū běn*) **deny** (*pǐ*).

Yellow not yellow—
**cannot** (*bù kě*) **align** (*yì*) with it.

**Preternatural** (*diān*) **spirits** (*líng*) **inversion** (*fǎn*), **times** (*shí*) **then have** (*yǒu*) **extremes** (*jí*).
**Mountain** (*gāng*) **erect** (*zhí*) **veiled** (*méng*) by the **head** (*qiú*), **thus exhausting** (*nǎi qióng*) the **divine realm** (*shén yù*).

What the **Heaven** (*tiān*) and **Earth** (*dì*) **cherish** (*guì*) is called **life** (*shēng*).
What **things** (*wù*) **revere** (*zūn*) is called **human** (*rén*).
